        "# Run vs. Walk Image Detector\n", 
        "This code creates a neural network that can detect whether an image is of a person walking or running. It uses the ResNet-50 neural network architecture which is available in PyTorch. ResNet was selected for this project because of its popularity and ResNet-50 (50 layers) was specifically selected because of its good balance between computational efficiency and performance." 
      ],

      "cell_type": "markdown", 
      "source": [ 
        "In these lines, \"criterion\" represents the loss function used to compute the difference between predicted and actual values during training.\n", 
        "\n", 
        "\"optimizer\" is the optimization algorithm that updates the resnet model's parameters based on the computed loss by the criterion, and it uses the Adam optimizer with a learning rate of 0.001 to control the size of parameter updates." 
      ], 
      "metadata": { 
        "id": "kEghxj4mtcp6" 
      } 
    }, 
    { 
      "cell_type": "code", 
      "source": [ 
        "from tqdm import tqdm\n", 
        "\n", 
        "for epoch in range(10):\n", 
        "    resnet.train()\n", 
        "    for inputs, labels in tqdm(train_loader):\n", 
        "        optimizer.zero_grad()\n", 
        "        outputs = resnet(inputs)\n", 
        "        loss = criterion(outputs, labels)\n", 
        "        loss.backward()\n", 
        "        optimizer.step()" 
      ],

        "In this code, the outer loop iterates over a specified number of training epochs, while the inner loop processes batches of the image data using the model. The tqdm library is used to create a progress bar that visually shows the progress of the inner loop, allowing you to monitor the training process. The training for 10 epochs of this model lasted roughly 67 minutes.\n", 
        "\n", 
        "The training process involves forward and backward passes through the model, loss computation, backpropagation to compute gradients, and parameter updates using the optimizer. This iterative process is how the model learns from the image training data to improve its performance."

        "## Testing Model" 
      ], 
      "metadata": { 
        "id": "pd0Urz1Iv2Mg" 
      } 
    }, 
    { 
      "cell_type": "code", 
      "source": [ 
        "resnet.eval()\n", 
        "correct = 0\n", 
        "total = 0\n", 
        "with torch.no_grad():\n", 
        "    for inputs, labels in test_loader:\n", 
        "        outputs = resnet(inputs)\n", 
        "        _, predicted = outputs.max(1)\n", 
        "        total += labels.size(0)\n", 
        "        correct += (predicted == labels).sum().item()\n", 
        "\n", 
        "accuracy = 100 * correct / total\n", 
        "print(f\"Test Accuracy: {accuracy:.2f}%\")" 
      ], 
      "metadata": { 
        "colab": { 
          "base_uri": "https://localhost:8080/"

      }, 
      "execution_count": 19, 
      "outputs": [

          "output_type": "stream", 
          "name": "stdout", 
          "text": [ 
            "Test Accuracy: 85.11%\n"

        }

      "cell_type": "markdown", 
      "source": [ 
        "This code sets the model to evaluation mode so that none of its layers are updated and their parameters remained fixed while running on the test set.\n", 
        "\n", 
        "The code then iterates through the test data, makes predictions using the model, and calculates the number of correct predictions and the total number of samples.\n", 
        "\n", 
        "Finally, it computes the accuracy by dividing the number of correct predictions by the total number of samples. An 85.11% accuracy is impressive considering total random classification would yield an accuracy of only 50%."
